3.  

Service Selection Board(SSB) 

Introduction 

              There are numerous ways of earning a Commission in Military, both for civilians 
(after 10+2, graduation, post graduation), as well as for serving personnel. Whatever be the 
mode, SSB is the step all have to clear, except for the medical corps. There is no limit on the 
number of attempts that can be made and the SSB Assessors encourage candidates to appear 
again for SSB.  
 
              The interview exercise is mainly a psychological assessment of the personality of the 
candidate, to gauge his/her potential as a future officer in Indian Military. The tests conducted 
by the SSB aim at selecting individuals with OLQs (Officer Like Qualities).  

 
 
              These qualities include effective intelligence, sense of responsibility, initiative, 
judgment (under stress), ability to reason and organize, communication skills, determination, 
courage, self-confidence, speed in decision-making, willingness to set an example, 
compassion and a feeling of loyalty to the nation.  
 
              Most of the tests require average intelligence. The SSB attempts to gauge the natural 
responses of the individuals. The tests are graded into various categories of both individual 
and group variety and each batch of candidates goes through the subtle testing pattern in the 
course of a few days. They are under observation not only while they perform in various 
psychological tests but even as they conduct themselves during the course of their stay at the 
SSB headquarters, where they are billeted for that duration.  
 
              The SSB Board is not concerned with the number of vacancies. Its responsibility is 
to assess and then, recommend. After recommendation, the candidates appear for Medical 

 



Examination and after that is the Merit List. Those who finally make the grade join for 
training and hence become Commissioned Officers. 

Procedure 

              The candidates who are declared by UPSC as having cleared the written exam, as 
well as those shortlisted in Direct Entries are called through Call Letters to appear for SSB 
(Allahabad/Bangalore/Bhopal/Dehradun/Mysore/Varanasi/) at the Centre allotted to the 
candidate. There have instances when the call-up letter fails to reach the candidate and the 
onus lies on the candidate to be alert and contact the office after a reasonable amount of time 
if the letter is not received when UPSC written has been cleared. Similar is the way for 
service candidates, except for that their movement is intimated to their seniors via movement 
orders. 

Day 0 (Day of Reporting) 

              SSB is a two stage process. To qualify for Stage II, a candidate needs to clear 
Screening Test or Stage I. On the date of reporting, the candidates are picked from the 
railway station and during the evening, certain Forms and also the Bio Data forms known as 

 Personal Information Questionnaire  (PIQ) are filled. PIQ is very important- there must 
be no cutting and consistency in each of the four or five copies of PIQ you are to fill. 

Day 1 (Screening Tests) 

              On the next day, is the Stage I, in which candidates are given Intelligence Test 
(Verbal and Non-Verbal), then there is a Picture Perception test, in which a slide (hazy or 
clear) is shown and then each candidate writes their story and later have a Group Discussion. 
This sequence is popularly called PPDT- Picture Perception and Discussion Test. After the 
completion of these tests, results are announced and those who do not make it in this attempt 
are dropped back to the railway station and the successful ones are retained for 4 days of 
detailed assessment. 

Day 2 (Psychology Tests) 

Thematic Appreciation Test (TAT)- Commonly known as Picture Story writing. 

 

Word Association Test (WAT) 

 

Situation Reaction Test (SRT) 

 

Self Description Test (SD), or a variation of this like description form the eyes of parents, 
teachers, colleagues, neighbors etc. 

 



 

Day 3 and Day 4 (GTO Tasks) 

Group Testing Officers (GTO) Test (Third and Fourth day)  
The following tests are conducted in this category.. 

Group discussion 

 

Group Planning Exercise (sometimes known as Military Planning Exercise) 

 

Progressive Group Tasks 

 

Half Group Tasks. 

 

Individual Obstacles 

 

Group Obstacles Race or Snake Race 

 

Command Task 

Lecturette 

 

Final Group Task 

 

Note:Interview :- (Held during afternoon/evening hours on 2nd/3rd/4th day) 

Day 5 (Conference) 

              On the final day, every Assessor and the candidate sit together for and have a chat- 
the fate of the candidate for that SSB is decided by the Assessors collectively there. The 
candidates are required to appear before the complete Board of Examiners comprising of 
President,Deputy President, all the psychologists, all the GTOs and Technical Officer. 
 
              After the Board Meeting of every candidate is over,the final result is declared within 

  an hour. Selected candidates are required to stay back for their medical examination (takes 

 



about 3 to 5 working days) in the Military Hospital near by or at a different place and the 
remaining candidates are dropped at the Railway Station. 

Details of the Tests 

The SSB follows a three-pronged approach consisting of three independent methods, by three 
different Officers to arrive at the most unbiased and objective conclusion:  
 
                           1.Purely psychological testing apparatus 
                           2.Outdoor test or group task officer's test 
                           3.Personal interview. 

PIQ Form: 

                On arrival at the SSB headquarters all candidates are given a questionnaire in 
which they have to fill in personal details regarding family background, educational profile 
etc. In addition this questionnaire is also a self-appraisal as some of the questions are aimed 
at gauging the candidate's opinion of him/her self. It forms a base for questions, which may 
be put to a candidate at the personal, interview stage and has importance for the psychologist 
on the Board which analyses the responses. 

Intelligence Tests: 

                Comprising both verbal and non-verbal questions are put to each candidate. It is in 
the form of a written test of the objective type with multiple-choice questions. Approximate 
time allotted for answering each question is 30 seconds. Candidates have to reason out the 
answers using common sense and intelligence on the basis of the facts given or pictures 
shown. It is presumed that a person of average intelligence does not lose the faculty of 
common sense reasoning even under pressure. Since time is important, candidates should 
leave the tricky questions for the last few minutes and attempt to answer the maximum 
number of questions. 

Word Association Tests (WAT): 

                This part of the psychological testing attempts to gauge the psychological make-up 
of the candidate on the basis of the responses of each candidate to words in everyday usage. 
As soon as a word is given a candidate is expected to formulate a sentence immediately. Only 
about 15 seconds are allowed to formulate each sentence and there are 60 words to be 
processed. 

Thematic Appreciation Test (TAT): 

                This again is a device to assess the outlook of a candidate through the medium of 
his/her responses to pictures or slides. About eight to ten such pictures are shown to the 
candidates for less than a minute and immediately after they are expected to write a small 
story based on the picture. Here again the thrust is on portraying positive traits of personality. 
The technique analyses the positive factors of the personalities of the candidates since it is 

 



felt that leaders of men can be built up from among those who already have inherent 
potential. The last slide is a blank slide, and it is often said that the psychologist reads the 
blank slide story first. 

Situation Reaction Tests (SRT): 

                The reaction of the candidates in response to everyday lifelike situations is 
analyzed. Certain instances, which may occur in the day-to-day life of ordinary individuals, 
are put to the candidates and they have to give their immediate reaction from among the 
multiple choices given. Answers are not rated in absolute terms of right or wrong; they are in 
fact weighted in the degree of correctness. Time for reaction is very short, approximately 30 
seconds and this is so because the Board wishes to analyze the spontaneous and natural 
responses of the candidates. 

Group Testing Officer (GTO) tasks: 

                The basic aim is to examine and observe candidates from close quarters in order to 
study their reactions to different tasks so as to analyze whether their thinking and responses 
on the individual plane (as revealed in the psychological testing system) tally with their 
actions in the groups tasks. There are a variety of tasks assigned in this phase.  
 
                Group discussion: A certain topic or situation is given to a group of candidates and 
they are expected to discuss the various aspects of the issue. It may be or may not be required 
to come to a decision on it, depending upon the instructions of the GTO. During the course of 
the group discussion the Group Task Officer observes each candidate- in his/her attitude as a 
member of the group, participation level, interaction with contemporaries, level of 
communication, reception to new ideas and view points alien to his/her own, ability to 
influence the group etc.  
 
                Lecturette: In this exercise each individual is given a choice of topics. Then each 
one is expected to speak on the chosen topic for 2-3 minutes during which his/her ability to 
speak extempore is observed and also the sequence of his thought processes. A logical, 
systematic sequence of thought, clarity of expression, way of holding oneself is all under 
review. A confident attitude, balanced views, easy flow and an easy stance are factors for 
success in this exercise. One should try not to fidget or move too much during the course of 
the lecture.  
 
                Group Planning: A model of a real life practical situation is presented to a group of 
candidates and they are asked to arrive at a plan of action. Initially they are asked to write 
down their own plan of action and thereafter they are expected to go over the different views 
and arrive at a consensus or group action plan. This exercise evaluates the analytical ability of 
the candidates, their ability to function in a group, appreciate the situation and plan 
accordingly. It gives an opportunity for the group to select a leader or for a leader to emerge 
in the group. Then it remains to be seen whether the leader can come up with the necessary 
qualities to carry the group towards a solution to the problem. Apart from leadership qualities 

 



this exercise also studies the group interaction level of each candidate.  
 
                Command Task: The exercise gives candidates an opportunity to assume command 
and get a task executed with the involvement of group members. The leader has to carefully 
select his/her team, assess the problem in hand and assign responsibilities to teammates. The 
exercise reveals the quality of leadership, the ability of a candidate to realize the potential of 
group members and the capacity to motivate others to accomplish a group activity. It is an 
exercise in alertness, tactical and administrative ability. It gives each one an opportunity to 
reveal his/her worth.  
 
                Individual Obstacles: In this exercise a candidate's level of physical fitness is 
gauged through a series of obstacles and activities such as rope climbing, climbing walls, 
jumping, etc. The activities are of varying levels of difficulty and performance as well as 
attitude of the candidate towards a difficult task is assessed. The SSB does not expect a 
candidate to accomplish every task or at the first attempt. On the basis of performance and 
attitude the candidate's level of physical fitness is evaluated.  
 
                Group Obstacles: Certain outdoor tasks are assigned to a group and they are 
expected to find a way out of the difficulties on the basis of group participation within the 
formulated rules. The exercise is an assessment of candidate participation in-group activities, 
planning and intelligent assessment of the situation put to the group. The Group Testing 
Apparatus thus reviews individual qualities in the context of a group. 

Personal Interview: 

                In this exercise the candidate is in direct conversation with the Interviewing Officer 
allotted to him/her. To put the candidate at ease, initial questions revolve around personal 
family background, hobbies, studies, friends, environment in which growing years have been 
spent.  
 
                The PIQ form of the candidate forms an important basis of the Interview. Some 
questions may relate to current happenings. Views on politics, religion, and nationalism may 
be sought from the candidate. Through real life situations the candidate's ability for common 
sense practical reasoning are analyzed. A balanced view with an intelligent assessment of the 
pros and cons is the best one.  
 
                Attitude towards family, friends, sports, games, hobbies, etc. are analyzed on the 
basis of the answers. In the interview a number of factors count apart from the actual verbal 
responses. The whole process of the interview right from the point of entering the room, 
manner of greeting, stance, courtesy, power of expression, attitude, manner of speaking, 
handling of difficult questions, objectivity of answers, manner of listening to a question are 
all under review and assessment.  
 
                Finally, One should never try to bluff or be inconsistent in views. A natural 

 



confident approach is the best. Ultimately it is the overall analysis of the individual's 
performance in the written examination in conjunction with the performance in the SSB tests. 
The list of recommended candidates are forwarded to the Medical Board. After clearing the 
Medical, and being successful in the Merit List, the candidate joins the training academy. For 
those who make it through this interesting challenge the future holds a lot of promise and 
national responsibility. 

Some General Points 

      1. Candidates appearing for the first time for a particular type of entry are paid 2nd class 
to-and-fro journey fare from the place of their residence to the place where they have come 
for the interview. 
      2. Accommodation and messing are free for the entire duration of their stay while 
undergoing SSB Tests. 
      3. The recommended Air Force candidates are required to go to a different place for 
medical examination on the specified date. 
      4. Air Force candidates who had applied for Pilot Entry have to first appear in Pilot 
Aptitude Battery Test(PABT). Those who are rejected in P.A.B.T cannot re-appear for Air 
Force Pilot entry again, but are welcome for other services and entries.

RECRUITMENT DRIVE OF NSS 

NSS Recruitment Drive: 
If we carefully observe our society we will find out that directly or indirectly this whole 

society is supporting to live our life smoothly whether it is an auto rickshaw driver or a 

former who is forming in field or the person who is cooking food for us in mess or our 

teacher, parents, friends etc. Each and every one of this society is playing a very important 

role in our life so being a Responsible Citizen of the Country It is our moral responsibility to 

do something (whatever we can) for the welfare of our society. 

The Objective of LPU-NSS is Development of Students personality and Moral value 

through Community Services.  Come and joint hands together to learn and enhance your 

own skill like Communication skill, Interpersonal skill, Leadership Quality etc. 

Register yourself @ https:tinyurl.com/(xxxxxxxx) 

For more Info Please Contact to: Mr. Ashok Singh (+91 8283877997 / 9041356513) 

Timeline for NSS Recruitment Drive: 

1.  Announcement on UMS from Aug 10 to Aug 20 (every year). 

2. Finalizing of Schedule of Student of their Interview and then messaging according 

to their schedule by UMS Messaging panel or SMS by Aug 22. 
th

3. Online Test* on 24  Aug. 

4. GD* of Student from Aug 25 to Aug 28 as per number of student. 
th

5. Personal Interview with Programme Officer / Coordinator on 29  Aug 

4. Compilation of result of personal interview by the interview panel on Aug 31. 

5. List of Result on UMS on Sep 01. 

6. Introduction cum orientation on Sep03 for all existing and new selected student. 

Code of Conduct:  All the volunteers who will be involve in Interview panel should 

be in appropriate formal dress code. 

 

*subject to no of student registered

Selection of the NSS Volunteer 

Selection of the LPU-NSS Volunteer 
The selection of the LPU-NSS Volunteer will be made by the Community Service Cell of the 
Division of Student Affairs in consultation with the Programme Coordinator /Head, Division 
of Student Affairs. 

Qualification 
1. NCC Cadet should not be appointed as NSS Volunteer. 
2. A student who is under disciplinary probation cannot be a NSS Volunteer. 
3. Final year Student is not eligible for the post of LPU-NSS Volunteer. 
4. A Volunteer can promote only one NSS Unit in an academic year 
5. A Volunteer must have a good academic record to become a NSS Volunteer. 
6. A Volunteer who has high level of, motivation, inclination and aptitude for 

community work. 
7. The students from foreign countries studying in Indian universities should also be 

encouraged to join NSS so that they may share the experiences of national 
reconstruction and community work. 

Selection Process 
As you are aware that the National Service Scheme (NSS) is the flagship programme of the 
Department of Youth Affairs under the Ministry of Youth Affairs and Sports 

1. Online registration compulsory for all Volunteers through UMS Link 
2. GD & PI 

 Tenure 
As a NSS Volunteer student need to complete 240 Hours in 2 Academic Year (as per NSS 
Hour Policy). The maximum period for NSS Volunteership is 2 year in the first instance. 
However, this period is extendible upto 3rd year, on the basis of the review of his/her 
performance by the Programme Officer and Programme Coordinator-Head, Division of 
Student Affairs. 
 

** NOTE: Already registered volunteers are required to renewal their registration again 

for every academic year. **

LPU NSS Volunteering Policy 
Every volunteer is expected to go through this policy and strictly adhere to them.  

1. All volunteers shall work under the guidance of a Coordinator / Co-Coordinator 
nominated by the Community Service Cell, Division of Student Affairs. 

2. Regularity and punctuality is a must thing that is expected in every volunteering 
opportunity. 

3. In case, any volunteer is not able to make up for the volunteering on a particular day 
(after the registration), then it is expected from the volunteer to inform the concerned 
person at least a day prior to the day of the volunteering. If any volunteer can‚Äôt do the 
same a strict action would be taken in such circumstances. 

4. In case of any conflict/issues regarding volunteering at the 
Event/NGOs/organizations, then the volunteers are expected to inform the Head, 
Community Service Cell, DSA, rather than having direct talks with 
NGO/Volunteers/Coordinators.  

5. While visiting any NGO or attending any event for volunteering, volunteers carry the 
Flexes/Standees of LPU-NSS and above all they represent Lovely Professional 
University, any kind of indiscipline would not be tolerated in any case. A strict action 
would be taken in such circumstances.  

6. While volunteering, volunteers are expected to devote their entire time in the 
volunteering, and shall not indulge in any other irrelevant activities.  

7. Any kind of discrepancies or proxies (both the people at fault) or tampering with the 
attendance record of volunteering will not be tolerated at all. Such actions are liable to 
the Disciplinary Committee.  

8. A Volunteer must attend at least on Special Camp/Mega Camp. 
9. A Volunteer must complete atleast 120 Hours in NSS (in one Academic Year) 
10. A Volunteer can promote only one NSS Unit in an academic year. 
11. Keep day to day records of activities/experiences in NSS diary and get it signed by 

programme officers. 
12. No Unit or any other NSS Meeting allowed without prior information to Head, 

Community Service Cell, DSA 
13. Wear NSS badge and University ID while on work. 
14. Not Separate whatsapp / Facebook group created for any event or Unit or any other 

purpose related to LPU-NSS. 
15. Dress Code:Proper Dress Code should be followed. 

 

LPU-NSS VOLUNTEERSHIP CANCELLED / DEBARD 

1. In case, any volunteer is not able to make up for the volunteering on a particular day 
(after the registration) or found guilty to fulfill any above said point. Strict action

Hours)

LPU-NSS Hours Policy 
This document is to clarify about the process of Hours and Hour Calculations. 
 
Hours Distribution 

 Hours to be completed are divided in three parts: Field Activities Hours, Campus 
Activities Hours and Regular volunteering Projects. 

 You can complete a maximum of 30 hours in Campus Activities type. More than 
30 hours won't be considered. 

 Say, you have 53Campus Activities Hours and 67 Filed Activities Hours / Regular 
Volunteering Projects, your total hours will be 97 instead of 120. 

 Maximum 6 hours counted in a Full day Event 
 Maximum 120 hours counted in one Academic year. 
 Maximum 240 Hours counted in 2 Years of Volunteership which include 50 

Compulsory Hours. 
 
Field Activities: (70 Hours) 

 Any  Regular activities conducted in adopted Villages/Slums (except any 
lecture/Seminars) 

 Awareness Rallies 
 Surveys 
 Activities under Sathi Project 
 Cleanliness Drive 
 Plantation Drive 
 Joy of giving (Distributions) 
 Joy of giving (Collections with prior approvals) 
 Social Events (Youthvibe / Vikrant, The LPU Social Fest / External Events within 

university) 
 Orphanage/Juvenilia/Old age home Visits 
 Drug De-addiction 

 
Campus Activities: (30 Hours) 

 Any guest lecture / Seminars / Training conducted by Community Service Cell, 
Division of Student Affairs. 

 Days Celebrations 
 Any hours devoted for Event Practices/Promotions. 
 Freshmen Induction. 
 Volunteering in any event organized by University (with Prior Written Approval 

of Community Service Cell)   
 Any event assign by Community Service Cell, Division of Student Affairs. 
 Fund Raising events 
 Unit meetings 
 RD Parade Practice 

 
Regular Volunteering Projects (20 Hours) 

 Computer Literacy Programme

Hours Complaint/Grievance 
 

Any type of grievance will be dealt by the programme officer only. If He/She fail to 
solve the grievance the case may be forwarded to the Programme Coordinator ‚Äì 
Head, Division of Student Affairs. 

Feel free to write to us at nss.csc@lpu.co.in for any kind of Hours Complaint/Grievance. 
 
Hours Authentications 

 Volunteers have to duly sign their dairies after the completion of Event form the 
Student Coordinator of respective unit/Event on same day. 

 Checking/Signing of NSS Diaries by programme officer will be done every 15 
days 

 Cross verification will be done by the Programme Coordinator once a Month.

Unit Coordinator or Co-coordinator 
Selection Policy 

Selection of the Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator 
The selection of the Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator will be made by the Community 
Service Cell of the Division of Student Affairs in consultation with the Programme 
Coordinator /Head, Division of Student Affairs. 

Qualification 
1. Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator will be selected from the Volunteers of LPU-

NSS only. 
2. NCC Cadet or OB Member of any Student Organization should not be appointed as 

NSS Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator. 
3. A student who is under disciplinary probation cannot be a Unit Coordinator or Co-

Coordinator. 
nd

4. 2  year* in LPU-NSS eligible for the post of Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator. 
5. A Volunteer can promote only one NSS Unit in an academic year 
6. A Volunteer must have a CGPA of 5.0 or more with no backlog to become a Unit 

Coordinator or Co-Coordinator. 
7. A Volunteer who has high level of, motivation, inclination and aptitude for 

community work and above all very good report with students should be preferred as 
Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator 

8. A Volunteer must attend at least on Special Camp/Mega Camp. 
9. A Volunteer must complete atleast 120 Hours in NSS (in one Academic Year) 
10.  A student who executes any new project under LPU-NSS may be given preference to 

become a Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator. 

Selection Process 
As you are aware that the National Service Scheme (NSS) is the flagship programme of the 
Department of Youth Affairs under the Ministry of Youth Affairs and Sports 

3. Online registration compulsory for all Volunteers through UMS Link 
4. Written Exam 
5. GD & PI 

Tenure 
The maximum period for which a Volunteer is appointed as Unit Coordinator or Co-
Coordinator will be 1 year in the first instance. However, this period is extendible upto 2nd 

9 | P a g e  
 



Version: 1.0, Dated: 01-07-2016 

year, on the basis of the review of his/her performance by the Programme Officer and 
Programme Coordinator-Head, Division of Student Affairs. 
If any Coordinator or Co-Coordinator found guilty in any disciplinary action their 
Coordination ship immediately cancelled. Any coordinator may be resigning from their 
coordinator ship in prescribed format (See Annexure-4) before the tenure with one month 
notice period. 

Functions of Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator 
The Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator will perform the following functions:- 

(a) He/she will plan the NSS regular activities and special camping programme as 
Programme guidelines issued by the Government of India and Community Service 
Cell, Division of Student Affairs. The Unit Coordinator or Co-Coordinator will ensure 
that NSS volunteers complete the prescribed hours in regular activities and participate 
in special camping programme as per requirements. The orientation of the NSS 
volunteers should be conducted in a befitting manner and hours should be devoted as 
per LPU-NSS Hours policy. 

(b) He/she will divide the NSS unit into different groups and assign the definite task and 
targets and projects (as per Allotted to their respective Unit) to each group. 

(c) He/she will work under the guidance of Head, Community Service Cell. 
(d) He/she will ensure that the basic aims of NSS Programme i.e. personality 

development of NSS volunteers, interaction of the different classes of society take 
place harmoniously and the NSS volunteers and community are benefited from the 
activities of NSS unit. 

(e) He/she will maintain the necessary records and registers prescribed by Community 
Service Cell, Division of Student Affairs.  

(f) He/she will hand over the charge of NSS Unit to Community Service Cell at the end 
of his/her tenure. 

(g) He/she may be Nominate NSS volunteers to Community Service Cell for participation 
in various programmes sponsored by the Department of Youth Affairs & Sports, 
Government of India such as National Integration Camps, Adventure Programmes, 
Republic Day Parade and any other function organised by the NSS Regional Centre. 

(h) He/she will submit the reports within 07 Days after the completion of 
Event/Activities. 

(i) He/she will also coordinate with the voluntary organizations working in the field of 
community development in general and youth work in particular. 

(j) He/She scrupulously avoid entering into any controversial issue. 
(k) In case of any conflict/issues regarding volunteering at the NGOs/organizations, then 

the Coordinator are expected to inform the Head, Community Service Cell, DSA, 
rather than having direct talks with NGO. 

(l) Any kind of discrepancies or proxies (both the people at fault) or tampering with the 
attendance record of volunteering will not be tolerated at all. Such actions are liable to 
the Disciplinary Committee.  

10 | P a g e  
 



Version: 1.0, Dated: 01-07-2016 

(m) While visiting any NGO for the volunteering, volunteers carry the Flexes/Standees of 
LPU-NSS and above all they represent Lovely Professional University, any kind of 
indiscipline would not be tolerated in any case. A strict action would be taken in such 
circumstances 

(n) In case, any volunteer is not able to make up for the volunteering on a particular day 
(after the registration), then it is expected from the coordinators to inform the head, 
Community Service Cell, DSA at least a day prior to the day of the volunteering. 

(o) Regularity and punctuality is a must thing that is expected in every volunteering 
opportunity. 

(p) Replacement of volunteers during any event is not allowed. 

LPU-NSS reserves the right to change the Selection Policy, at any point in time, without any prior intimation.

NSS-Spl-Camp-Guidelines 
Special Camp provides a unique opportunity to the NSS student youth for group living, 
mutual understanding, tolerance, cohesion, development of leadership qualities, bringing out 
the hidden talents of the students, etc.  To make constructive use of students‚Äô leisure time for 
community work, these camps may be organized during the vacation i.e. Summer/Winter.  
During the Special Camp, the students should stay with the communities (Adopted Villages) 
where they are holding the camps.  The duration of a Special Camp is generally Seven days. 
The following are the broad guidelines to be followed by the NSS Units.  These guidelines 
are discussed under 3 broad heads viz., I) Pre-Camp preparation, II) During Special Camp, 
and III) Post Special Camp requirements.  
 
1.  PRE-CAMP PREPARATION:  This phase involves from the submission of camp 
proposal to the starting day of the camp. 
 

1.1   Submission of Camp Proposal:  The LPU-NSS Coordinator or Co coordinator or 
Volunteer of Units is required to submit the Special Camp proposal at least four weeks in 
advance so as to ensure the approval of camp well in time.  The proposal should be submitted 
in the prescribed proforma, which is enclosed along with these guidelines (see Annexure-2).  
The proposal should contain the Sarpanch Consent, Venue Pics, Approx budget, route map 
and day-wise programme. 

1.2   Selection of Proper Project: The selection of proper project for Special Camping 
programme can boost up the morale of campers and develop in them a sense of achievement.  
Hence, it is essential that suitable project for the personality development of NSS volunteers 
must be selected with utmost care by identifying the felt needs of the community.  Without 
participation of local community, the camp has no value. The following should be kept in 
mind while selecting the project. 

ÔÉò Identifying the felt needs of the community such as health, education, environmental 
social and economic development of the community. 

ÔÉò Accommodation, water facilities available in the community to the volunteers should 
be assessed before camp. 

ÔÉò It is essential to make sure of the participation of the community in the projects. 
ÔÉò LPU-NSS Coordinator or Co coordinator or Camp Coordinator of Units is directed to 

see that the selected projects should be completed within 7 days the camping period of 
7 days.  If for any reason, the project is not completed in 7 days, the same should be 
undertaken during the regular activity as a follow-up action. 

 

1.3 Selection of NSS Volunteers for Special Camp: LPU-NSS Coordinator or Co 
coordinator of Units or Camp Coordinator is hereby informed to take the necessary care 
while selecting the volunteers for the 7 days camp.  It is fair and proper to give preference to 
the NSS volunteers, who have contributed their service during the regular activities. 

12 | P a g e  
 



Version: 1.0, Dated: 01-07-2016 

a) Each camp should consist of Minimum 35 NSS volunteers, local community Youth 
and 1 Programme Officer and Maximum 100 NSS volunteers.  The list of participants 
along with their willingness may be sent to office of Community Service Cell, 
Division of Student Affairs along with the proposal. 

b) The LPU-NSS Coordinator or Co coordinator of Units or Camp Coordinator should 
ensure adequate representation of NSS volunteers from BC/SC/ST communities and 
Girl volunteers. 

 
1.4 Information to the concerned District Collector about the Camp: 
 

a) Once the camp dates are finalized, the Programme Officer or Camp Coordinator is 
required to inform the camping dates requesting the District Collector to extend 
necessary cooperation of other District Officers such as District Medical & Health 
Officer, District Agricultural (Extension) Officer, District Field Publicity Officer, 
District Veterinary Officer, District Youth Welfare Officer and Nehru Yuva Kendra 
Coordinator, etc., in the district. 

b) The Programme Officer or Camp Coordinator is directed to meet the District Officers 
in person requesting their cooperation for a successful completion of the camp. 

c) The Programme Officer or Camp Coordinator may involve local voluntary 
organizations such as Lion/Rotary and other N.G.O‚Äôs, etc. 

 
1.5   Orientation:  LPU-NSS Camp Coordinator is required to give necessary organization to 
the volunteers about the 7 days programme.  To keep up the dignity of University to which 
they belong and for smooth functioning of the camp rules and regulations should be clearly 
mentioned in the orientation meeting. 

2.       DURING SPECIAL CAMP: 
 
2.1  The Programme Officer/ Camp Coordinator must follow the day-wise programme 
 scrupulously. 
2.2  Strict discipline must be adhered by the volunteers during Special Camp. 
2.3  Activities and Programme must be taken up as per the guidelines and the special camp 

 theme. 
2.4  The Programme Officer/ Camp Coordinator is directed to maintain a separate 

attendance register for the 7 days camp which will be verified by the University NSS 
personnel.  

2.5  The Programme Officer/ Camp Coordinator is also informed to maintain a Cash Book 
for the 7 days camp and it should be made available for the programme personnel from 
the  University to go through the same. 

2.6  The Programme Officer/ Camp Coordinator is directed not to leave the camping place 
 leaving the camp responsibility to the NSS volunteers.  In this connection, the 
Programme Officers/ Camp Coordinator may also take the assistant of other staff 
members of the  University. 

2.7  It is also important to note that the volunteers should present all the 7 days in the 
camp.  It is imperative as and when any NSS personnel from University visit the camp, 
they will not down the strength of the campers. Accordingly, the camp grant will be 
limited. Certificates are also issued only to the members present in the camp (For all 
Seven Day). 

13 | P a g e  
 



Version: 1.0, Dated: 01-07-2016 

2.7.1 The Camp Coordinator must exhibit at least two NSS Banners in a ‚Äòstandard size‚Äô one 
should be fixed at the camping place and another should be at a conspicuous place in 
the village. 

3.    POST CAMP REQUIREMENTS:   
Immediately after completion of the camp, the following items should be submitted to the 
University. 
 
3.1 Submission of Accounts and Reports:  Camp Coordinator is informed that the Special 

Camp reports and accounts should be submitted to the Community Service Cell, 
Division of Student Affairs within 10 days after completion of the camp. 

 
3.2 The statement of accounts along with Bills in original should be submitted separately, 

and the report along with action photos, press clippings, etc., should be submitted in a 
Book form. 

 
3.3 List of NSS volunteers participated in the camp should be sent in the following 

proforma, in triplicate. 
 
S.No. Name of the Gender Category Contact Signature 

Volunteer No 
1 to   OC/BC/SC/ST   
100 
   

3.4 Participants‚Äô experiences should be reviewed and a consolidated report on their 
experiences should be submitted to the office of community Service Cell, Division of 
Student Affairs. 

4.    Administration of the Camp:  
1. All NSS volunteers participating in the camp should be divided into different groups. 

Each one will undertake activities according to one‚Äôs aptitude, educational 
qualification and skill. 

2. All the Volunteers should strictly abide by the camp rules and stay in the camp. It is 
suggested that the following Committees may be formed for running the camp :- 
 Overall Student Camp Coordinator: NSS Coordinator or Co-Coordinator of 

any Unit may be eligible for the Overall Student Camp Coordinator; all other 
committees are report to them. 

 Mess Committee: It will look after the food arrangements of the camp. Preparing 
budgets, tie ups with vendors, seeking quotations and maintaining record of 
transactions. Drafting of approvals required for the sanctioning of funds. They 
will have to ensure a sufficient and healthy food for the members and for the 
visitors during the camp. The quality and quantity of food must be kept up to the 
standards by the committee members. Surprise and regular checks must be in 
practice to ensure the smooth functioning of the committee. 

 .Programme Committee: To conduct the day-to-day activities of the camp. 
Exploring the opportunities available inside and outside the campus. Short listing 
and finalizing the venues with valid reasons. The will have to ensure that all 
volunteers are treated equally and counter check that the number of volunteers are

not repeated for tasks and activities assigned. Approvals regarding duty leaves to 
the volunteers and non-volunteers will be recorded and managed by program 
committee. 

 Project Committee: To take care of the project work including supply of tools 
and equipment. 

 Cultural Programme Committee: To arrange the cultural programmes in the 
way that all participants get opportunity to show their skill and talent. Group 
performance may be given preference over individual performance. Cultural 
events may include: rallies, promotional lectures, one act play, inspirational 
videos at socio joints, flash mob, posters, flexes, brochure, pamphlets, logos, 
sticker‚Äôs, or any other creative things to mark the presence of NSS whenever and 
where required. They will have to ensure that prior approval is taken by the 
program officer before the conduct of any event by the committee. 

 General Discipline Committee: It will look after the discipline in the camp. 
 Reception and Guest Committee: It will look after the guests in the camp, and 

make necessary arrangements for their arrival and departure. Proper dress code 
and drill will be followed by the committee. 

 Sponsorship Committee: It will look after the sponsors form inside and outside 
the campus. Generating funds for the existing and future NSS activities, 
Formation of plans and policies for vendor‚Äôs sponsorship so as to ensure a win 
win situation for both NSS and Vendors. Maintaining a proper record of all 
vendors and informing them regarding their existence and presence during the 
commencement of the event. 

 Budget Committee:  
a. It will look after all the purchase/Cash during camp. 
b. Account keeping by verifying each & every bill before putting up to the head. 
c. Settle accounts within 2 weeks of concluding of Camp  
d. To make record of all the consumable & non-consumable articles

 NSS Advisory Committee Policy 
The NSS Advisory Committee at University Level will be an apex body as far as 
implementation of NSS at University Level is concerned. LPU-NSS set up an NSS Advisory 
Committee to advice on programme planning and development under the Chairmanship of 
the Vice-Chancellor. It will review the NSS activities in the area of the University and ensure 
allocation of NSS student‚Äôs strength and review the work done by all the Units. 

Composition of University Advisory Committee - NSS 
1. Vice Chancellor     - Chairmanship 
2. Head, Division of Student Affairs   - Member Secretary 
3. Programme Officers     - Executive Member 
4. NSS Volunteer (Max 4 Volunteers)   - Members 
5. NSS Alumni  (2 Volunteers)    - Alumni Member 

Frequency of meetings 
The University Advisory Committee should meet at least twice a year to review, plan and 
monitor the NSS activities.  

Role & Responsibility 
This committee should concentrate on the following issues: - 
(a)  Review and progress of the NSS during the previous year;   
(b)  Formulation of the plans for NSS programmes and activities to be undertaken during the 
current year;  
(c)  Approval of the allocation to be made to the NSS units during the current year; 
(d)  Approval of special projects to be undertaken during the year. 
(e)  Review / Reallocate the NSS Unit to the Volunteers. 
(f)  The outstanding work of the NSS volunteers of the unit should be recognized by 
awarding special certificates. The work of such volunteers should be brought to the notice of 
NSS Regional Centre of concerned region.

NSS 240 Hours Certificate Policy 
LPU-NSS Volunteers who have completed 240 Hours in Social Service during 2 year and 
work under different Social Projects along with participation in one weeklong (seven days' 
and night) camp under special camping programme are eligible for NSS Certificate & 
Trophy. 
In addition, NSS volunteers also honoured at university level for their excellent and 
outstanding work in NSS. 

Process for Certificate Apply:   
 

th
LPU-NSS Volunteer required submitting their duly filled NSS Dairy before 30  April to the 
Programme Officer along with the reports of their work done during their 240 Hours in 
Prescribed format (See annexure-1) given by Community Service Cell, Division of Student 
Affairs.

GUIDELINES FOR NSS 240 HOURS AWARD 

1. A student should have completed a minimum of two years of volunteership in NSS. 
2. He/she should have participated in at least one Special Camp or participated in one of 

the National Programmes like R.D. Parade Camp in Delhi, National Integration 
Camps, Mega Camps, National Youth Convention, Suvichar, National Youth Festival, 
Programmes under RGNIYD,Inter-State Youth Exchange Programmes, Adventure 
Programmes,etc. sponsored by the Ministry of Youth Affairs and Sports. 

3. He/she should have completed 240 hours of community service during two 
consecutive years of volunteership. 

4. His/her academic performance should have been reasonably good.

NSS Coordinator 

Lovely Professional University

3page 



The Student Employment Services in Lovely Professional University 

 

This manual shall be called ‚ÄòStudent Employment Services Manual‚Äô. 

1.0 Objective 

Lovely Professional University provides part time job opportunities to its students to explore 
their immense potential and expose them to the world of work before actual employment. This 
would also help the students to participate in the management and development of the 
University, inculcating among them social values like dignity of labor, sense of belongingness, 
self dependence and hard work. 

The students would be paid for these jobs and after satisfactory completion of the assigned job, 
the students will be issued appreciation Letters. 

2.0 Eligibility: 
2.1 All the regular students of Lovely Professional University who are registered in the 

current term and are not admitted in a programme/course with duration of less than 
six months are eligible to apply. 

2.2 Certain CGPA could be applied as an eligibility criterion as per the requirement of 
job.  

 

3.0 Tenure of these jobs: 
3.1 The recruitment for these jobs will be done for a term or for the complete project 

whichever is earlier. 
3.2 The recruitment shall be done as and when the requirement arises in any department/ 

cell of the university.  

 

4.0 Nature and Description of Jobs:  

Jobs which are offered by the University are divided into four categories. 

4.1. Category I : For M.Phill/Phd/Masters(optional): Rs 150/- per lecture; Rs 250 per 
Tutorial; Rs 6500/- per month, the jobs in category I require formal education in the 
particular discipline, work experience and/or a minimum standard of achievement. 

4.2. Category II: For Masters: Rs 55/- per hour; the jobs in category II require formal 
education in the particular discipline, work experience and/or a minimum standard of 
achievement. 

4page 



4.3. Category III: For Bachelors: Rs 50/- per hour; the jobs in category III require formal 
education in the particular discipline, work experience and/or a minimum standard of 
achievement. 

4.4. Category IV: Rs 45/- per hour; the jobs in category IV do not require formal education 
in the particular discipline, work experience and/or a minimum standard of achievement. 

Jobs in Category

Departments/ Cells. 

5.0 Job Notifications 
5.1 The department who wants to offer such jobs to the students will first draft a proposal 

to be submitted to DSA. The proposal will contain the Job Description, Job 
Specification, Terms and Conditions, Selection criteria, Selection panel and Selection 
process for the job. The format of the proposal is attached at Annexure I. The 
soliciting department is requested to add content as per its specific requirement. 

5.2 The department shall ensure that employment of the student does not compromise 
confidentiality or internal secrecy of the department & the University as a whole. 

5.3  The drafted proposal shall be forwarded to the Office of DSA at least 2 Week before 
the start of the job 

5.4 DSA will study the feasibility of jobs mentioned in the proposal and within one week 
seek approval from the Office of the Pro Chancellor.  

5.5 The job will be given a job ID No. 
5.6 After approval, the DSA will notify on the UMS details of the student jobs for timely 

selection of the students and offering their services to the concerned Department. 

 

6.0 Selection Process: 
6.1 Interested students need to apply online on the prescribed application form. It must be 

noted that student may apply if they want to serve a certain slot time equal to or less 
than but inclusive in the asked time slot. For example, if the asked time slot is 2 PM 
to 5 PM, the student may apply if he is available for 3 PM to 4 PM (Annexure II) 

6.2 The selection process shall be proposed by the solicitor department. Division of 
Student Affairs will finalize the process, date, time and venue (preferably the 
Division of Student Affairs premises) for the selection process. A nominee of Pro-
Chancellor office shall be appointed by Pro-Chancellor as a member of the selection 
panel. DSA may appoint a representative to oversee the matters from administrative 
and procedural perspective.  

6.3 As per the selection process designed by the Solicitor department, candidates may be 
short listed by the Selection committee on the basis of their application forms and 
CVs and the shortlisted students shall be called to attend the selection process. The 
notification inviting the shortlisted candidates must contain an Instructions sheet 

7page 



containing the expectations from candidates during the process. The Instruction sheet 
may contain Rules during selection process, Items and testimonials to be presented 
during the process, Timings of the process etc as applicable for the particular process. 

6.4 The Solicitor Department should consider requirement of keeping additional 
candidates on reserve panel to meet any future requirement that may arise due to a 
student leaving a job.  

6.5 Selection Committee will then conduct the selection process  and  fill the Student 
Assessment Sheet.(Annexure III) 

6.6 Student Assessment sheets of all the experts will be sent to DSA. The list will be 
finalized by the DSA after taking the security clearance of the candidates from the 
department of security and discipline. 

6.7 The list of selected candidates along with the applicable terms and conditions shall be 
presented for approval to Pro-Chancellor by DSA. (Annexure IV and V) 

6.8 The copy of the approval, list of selected students and Terms and conditions shall be 
forwarded to AO of solicitor department and Department of Accounts for salary 
disbursement matters. 

6.9 The selected candidates will be inducted into the job after taking an undertaking of 
understanding and acceptance of the nature of job, working hours, no. of days and all 
other terms and conditions.  

6.10 The Department of work will complete the Student Employee weekly Job Roster 
as per Annexure VI and submit one copy to the DSA for records. 

 
7.0  Work Place:  

7.1 Job sites available within LPU campus or any place decided by LPU from time to 
time. 

 
8.0  Working Hours: 

8.1 During the term when the academic session is going on, a student is recommended to 
opt a maximum of 4 hrs a day subject to the maximum of 20 hrs in a week. However, 
if the student employee is available for time more than recommended time limits he 
may be allowed by Reporting Official by taking written approval from Head, 
Division of Student Affairs.   In any case a student cannot opt for more than 8 hrs a 
day. 

8.2 In case the Department wishes to change the mode of work as defined in Annexure I 
the same could be done by submitting and Application to the DSA and on approval 
can implement the change.  

8.3 The time recorded in the attendance register shall be a multiple of 10 minutes. Total 
time devoted by a student employee in a month will be calculated by adding up each 
single entry without rounding off and the sum will be rounded off to the floor 
multiple of 1 hour to find the devoted time in terms of hours only. 

9.0  Salary Structure: 
9.1 Students working in jobs of Category I: Rs 35/- per Hour. 
9.2 Students working in jobs of Category II: Rs 25/- per Hour. 

 

8page 



 
 
 
10.0 Responsibilities of Reporting official 

10.1 To take for record CV of the student employee mentioning Name, Registration 
number and contact no. and containing details about Academic achievement, Co-
curricular achievements, projects etc. 

10.2 To take in hard and soft copy the Time-Table of student to know the available 
free slots in which student can make himself/ herself available. 

10.3 To take Account no. of the account of Student Employee for disbursement of 
salary. 

10.4 To design the Student Employment Job Roster. 

10.5 To note attendance of student employee in the provided format. 

10.6 To take over the work done by student employee at the end of each shift.  

11.0 Marking Attendance and payment: 
11.1 The Reporting Officer will record the attendance of the students. 
11.2 An attendance Register shall be maintained by reporting official for the record of 

attendance. A new page shall be opened for each new student employee according to 
format provided in Annexure VII. 

11.3 The record of the attendance shall be handed over to concerned AO of the 
department. 

11.4 The AO of the concerned Department will compile the Salary Sheet (as per 
Annexure VIII) of the students at the end of every month or at the time of relieving of 
student employee, whichever comes earlier and will forward the compiled attendance, 
Attendance record along with the approved terms and conditions to Department of 
Audit for auditing. 

11.5 The audited sheet of student employees‚Äô attendance record shall be forwarded to 
Pro-Chancellor for approval. The approved copy shall be forwarded to Department of 
Accounts for crediting the emoluments in the account of the student employees. 

11.6 The salary will be disbursed within first 15 days of every month in case of 
continued service or within 15 days of relieving of student employee, whichever 
applicable. 

11.7  

12.0 Leave Policy: 
12.1 A student should be very careful in choosing the time slot according to his/her 

own schedule. 

9page 



12.2 A student should not commit the time slots at the cost of his/her classes as no 
compensation in the form of attendance or any other component of continuous 
assessment will be provided. 

12.3 If a student has already committed for the availability for a time slot and later on 
is unable to come ,then he must take leave at least one day prior to the date of leave 
by filling the leave form(Annexure IX) 

12.4 Post dated leaves are strictly discouraged among the students. 
12.5 If a student is unable to reach at the specified place and at the specified time, then 

he must intimate his/her unavailability to the Reporting Official telephonically and 
must fill the Post Dated leave format within 48 hrs. of the leave.(Annexure IX) 

12.6 All the Pre & Post dated leaves will be sanctioned by the DSA only and DSA will 
keep record of all Post dated leaves of the students employed on such Jobs.  

12.7 In case a student is on leave without intimation, then he would be treated as 
ABSENT WITHOUT INFORMATION and such conduct may lead to the termination 
of the services. Reporting Official shall be responsible to intimate DSA about such 
cases within 24 Hrs of the incident and DSA will keep track of all such cases and may 
debar the student from appearing in subsequent recruitment processes for Part-Time 
jobs. 

13.0 Appraisal & Feedback 
13.1 At the time of completion of job or term whichever is earlier, Reporting Officer is 

required to fill the Appraisal & Feedback form of all the students (Annexure X). 
13.2 This form must be filled within the seven working days of relieving of the 

student. 
13.3 DSA will be responsible for keeping track of appraisal of students and will use the 

information in case the student is recruited again. 
13.4 DSA shall, time to time, confirm upon the optimum utilization of student 

employees by cross-checking the workload and related documentation and by 
physically visiting the job site. 

14.0 Exit Policy 
14.1 A student should book the job slots according to his/her availability but if due to 

some unforeseen circumstances he is not able to continue the job then he/she must 
request DSA  to cancel further slots. 

14.2 In such case, an exit form (Annexure XI) must be submitted in the office of DSA 
after obtaining remarks of Reporting authority giving a notice period of One Week. 

14.3 A student will be relieved from the job at the end of the term or the completion of 
the project whichever is earlier. 

14.4 Student employee shall have to obtain the No dues certificate and submit it in the 
office of DSA on his/her last working day. (Annexure XII) 

14.5 Students are strictly advised to complete all the formalities at the time of 
relieving, failing which shall debar them from obtaining appreciation letter and the 
same will be considered as an act of indiscipline and shall be dealt accordingly. 

10page 



14.6 An Employment experience certificate shall be provided to the Student Employee 
at the time of relieving from the job, if the student employee has devoted at least 100 
man hours on the job from the time of appointment.  

14.7 A student employee shall not be provided certificate in the following cases, 
14.7.1 If the tenure of the job is less than 100 man hours. 
14.7.2 If the Student Employee is suspended from the job due to low level 

of performance or due to deviant workplace behavior. 
14.7.3 If the Student Employee is under disciplinary probation. 

14.8 Student Employee may ask a provisional certificate during the tenure of job, if 
required. The Student Employee shall have to submit a written application to the 
Reporting Officer.  

14.9 The Reporting Officer shall forward all the related requests to Division of Student 
Affairs, who then shall issue the certificates. 

15.0 Filling Vacancies arising due to Exit of student 
15.1 Vacancy arising due to exit of a student employee can be filled in by the DSA 

along with the consent of concerned department by following ways: 
15.1.1 Appointing students who are already working and meeting the 

requirements of the job. 
15.1.2 Notifying the job on the UMS and following the complete process 

of recruitment all over again. 

16.0 Responsibility of student as an employee 
16.1 The student employee is required to be punctual and regular. 
16.2 The student employee should always work with the aim of improving work 

efficiency and organizational development. 
16.3 The student employee should be a good team member. 
16.4 The student employee should judiciously utilize the resources of the organization. 
16.5 The student employee should be loyal to his/her work and maintain 

confidentiality of the work assigned to him. 
16.6 The student employee should maintain proper decorum at his/her work place.

NSS CERTIFICATE POLICY
=====================================================================
Chapter 1 
 

NSS Certificate Policy 
 

The main aim of this policy is to establish guidelines for certificates issued in recognition of LPU-NSS 
Volunteers for the Social Work done under the National Service Scheme, Ministry of Youth Affairs & 
Sports organized in Adopted Village, Slums and within the University premises. The formats used for 
certificates are established by the level of NSS Hours Completed by the NSS Volunteers. The various 
levels of Certificate are mentioned below: 

1.1 Background of Certificate on the basis of type of Categories 
1.1.1 ‚ÄúA‚Äù Grade Certificate (Sample 1): The "A‚Äù Grade certificate will be awarded to the 

NSS Volunteers who fulfil the following eligibility Criteria. 
 
Compulsory Points 

ÔÉº Volunteer have completed at least 120 Hours in one Academic Year 

ÔÉº Attended at least one Seven Day Camp 

ÔÉº Donated Blood or Motive the peoples to donate the Blood. 

 
Participated in at Least 50% Activities (In Addition to the above Said Points) 

ÔÉº Swachh Bharat Abhiyan 

ÔÉº Legal Awareness Programmes 

ÔÉº Tree Plantation Drive 

ÔÉº Health Awareness Programme

1.2 Guidelines for Printing and distribution of Certificates to be awarded 
i. Blank Certificates shall be retained by Record Cell, Division of Examination with a minimum 

stock of 500 copies all the time and will order a fresh lot of 200 copies, in case the stock falls 
below the mentioned number. 

ii. The host Department/ Division requesting printing of certificates shall forward a request on hard 
copy, duly approved by head of respective Division, to Record Cell in the format prescribed in 
Annexure I at least 7 days before the day of distribution of certificates.  

iii. The Content of certificate as per Category only. Field that must be covered in certificates to be 
awarded to students of Lovely Professional University are: 

a. Title of Certificate 
b. Serial No. 
c. Name  
d. Father/ Husband Name 
e. Registration No. 
f. Programme and year 
g. Date of Issuance of certificate 
h. Place of Issuance 
i. Signature of Record Cell official 
j. Signature of Verifying and Authorizing Officials 

 
k. ‚ÄòFather/ Husband Name‚Äô, ‚ÄòRegistration No.‚Äô and ‚ÄòProgramme and Year‚Äô listed in iv., v. 

and vi. are mandatory only if the event/ activity is applicable only to students of Lovely 
Professional University. In all other cases, these fields shall be included considering 
applicability and requirement of the fields.  

l. Sample content of certificate is provided in Annexure I, II & III and design standards is 
provided in Sample 1, 2 3.  

iv. The authenticity of data provided to Record Cell shall be the sole responsibility of host 
Department and Record Cell will not be accountable for the validity of the data. 

v. Record Cell will print the certificates as requested providing a unique Serial number to each 
certificate and will keep the lot ready to dispatch at least 1 day prior to the day of distribution.  

vi. Once the lot of printed certificates is ready for dispatch, Record Cell will forward email 
requesting the host department to collect the printed certificates at official email id of the host 
Department/ Division. 

vii. The host Department/ Division shall collect the lot immediately after receiving the information 
regarding the printed status of certificates.  

viii. Record Cell will maintain record of all the dispatched certificates. 
ix. Host Department/ Division will distribute the certificate and will record the receipt of certificate 

by recipient of certificate.  
x. Host Department/ Division will send the record of receipt of certificates to Record Cell, which 

further shall maintain a record of receipt of certificates. 
xi. Any certificate that is not awarded due to absence of recipient of certificate will be sent back to 

Record Cell along with the record of receipt of certificates. Such certificates shall be kept safe by 



Record Cell and will be awarded, in case the recipient of certificate appears to collect the 
certificate later. 

xii. Record Cell, if receives a request asking for re-issuance of a certificate, shall maintain the data 
for the re-issued certificates. A certificate shall be re-issued on payment of 500/-. Re-issued 
certificate shall bear a stamp of ‚ÄòDuplicate copy‚Äô.  

 
Chapter 2

presence and contribution has been considered significant by Organizing Committee or Done an 
extraordinary work in field of Social Work. Following rules and guidelines shall be applicable: 

i. The process of printing ‚ÄòLetter of Appreciation‚Äô shall be 
a. The request for printing shall be sent to Department of Brand Development in the format 

provided in Annexure IV. Sample design is provided in Annexure V. 
b. The request along with the designed format shall be sent for approval to Head, Division of 

Student Welfare. 
c. Approved design shall then be sent for printing.

POLICY  FOR  OFF-CAMPUS  PARTICIPATION  BY  STUDENTS  OF  LOVELY

PROFESSIONAL UNIVERSITY

1. Off-Campus Participation

Off-campus  participation  in  this  policy  means  participation  in  an  Academic/  co-

curricular/  Cultural/  Sports/  Community  welfare  activity/  Entrepreneurship/Startup

event/Competition that is to be conducted outside University Campus and by an agency/

Institute/ University other than Lovely Professional University and its affiliated bodies.

2. Facilitation to students

2.1 University endeavors to facilitate students for off-campus participation by providing

Funds, Duty leaves and other such provisions that are required for such participations.

2.2 Students  are  required  to  take  prior  written  permission  for  participating  in  an off-

campus  event.  There may be cases  in  which  the  students  may not  be allowed to

represent the University in an event. Participation without prior permission shall be

considered as an act of indiscipline and shall be dealt accordingly. 

2.3 Students who are under disciplinary probation may not participate in an off-campus

event. Student who had been involved in any act of indiscipline in past shall have to

Page | 3 



mention  the  same in  application  and may be  sent  only  on the  discretion  of  Pro-

Chancellor.

2.4 To define the extent of facilitation, following categories are recognized:

2.4.1 Category I: Fully funded events with duty leaves: - This category includes

International Events, National level Inter-University fests like Association of

Indian  Universities  Youth  Fest  and  Sports  meet.   In  this  category  all  the

expenses are incurred by the University.  The policies  related to the events

falling  under  this  category  are  mentioned  in  the  manuals  of  Division  of

Student Welfare.  

Pro-chancellor may add any other event to this category anytime either suo-

moto or on recommendations of a DOD, a HOF or Head, Division of Student

Welfare.

2.4.2 Category II: Partially funded events with duty leaves: - In this category, a

part of the expense will be incurred by University depending upon the impact

and brand value of event and the competencies of performers. Event may be at

any level.

2.4.3 Category III: Non-Funded with duty leaves:- In this case, the students will

be provided only duty leaves but not any financial support for participation. 

2.4.4 Category IV: Non-Funded without duty leaves:- This category includes all

the cases in which University allows student to participate but do not provides

any facilitation in terms of funds or duty leaves.

3. Norms for off-campus participation for partially funded and Non-Funded with duty

leaves events:

3.1  Application Rules

3.1.1 Student will have to submit the application for participation at least 10 days before

leaving for the event. Annexure I

3.1.2 The authorities for initiating, recommending and sanctioning of the application

are as follows:
Page | 4 



Initiated by Recommended by Sanctioned by

Cultural Any  Faculty Cultural Participation Committee Pro-Chancellor

Staff Member

Sports Any  Faculty Sports Participation Committee Pro-Chancellor

Staff Member

Academic/  Co- Any  Faculty Academic Participation Committee Pro-Chancellor

curricular Staff Member
Entrepreneurship Entrepreneurship Participation Committee Pro-Chancellor

Event / Startup Pitch Coach

Details of committees are mentioned in section 3.1.3

3.1.3 All  participations  shall  be  Recommended  by  Participation  Committee  as

mentioned below

3.1.3.1 All Cultural Events including Theatre, Literary, Fine Arts, Music and Dance

event  participation  shall  be  recommended  by  Cultural  Participation

Committee  which includes  (list  mentions  the name in descending order  of

signature and remarks required)

3.1.3.1.1 Head, Division of Student Welfare

3.1.3.1.2 Head, Student Affairs Planning Cell

3.1.3.1.3 Head, Department of Cultural Affairs

3.1.3.1.4 Respective School Cultural Coordinator

3.1.3.2 All Sports events participation shall be recommended by Sports Participation

Committee  which includes  (list  mentions  the name in descending order  of

signature and remarks required)

3.1.3.2.1 Head, Division of Student Welfare

3.1.3.2.2 Head, Student Affairs Planning Cell

3.1.3.2.3 Head, Department of Sports

3.1.3.2.4 Respective School Sports Coordinator
Page | 5 



3.1.3.3 All Academic Events including Academic, co-curricular, research, workshops

etc.  event  participation  shall  be  recommended  by  Academic  Participation

Committee  which includes  (list  mentions  the name in descending order  of

signature and remarks required)

3.1.3.3.1 Head, Division of Research

3.1.3.3.2 DOD/ HOS

3.1.3.3.3 HOD/ COD

3.1.3.3.4 School Research Coordinator

3.1.3.3.5 Class  Incharge/  Training  and  Placement  Coordinator/  Any  staff  or

faculty member

3.1.3.4 The  events  that  do  not  fall  in  any of  the  above  three  categories  shall  be

recommended  by  Special  Committee  for  Off-Campus  participations  which

includes (list mentions the name in descending order of signature and remarks

required)

3.1.3.4.1 Head, Division of Student Welfare

3.1.3.4.2 Head, Student Affairs Planning Cell

3.1.3.4.3 Head, Department of Sports

3.1.3.4.4 Head, Department of Cultural Affairs

3.1.3.4.5 Any initiating Faculty/ Staff Member

3.1.3.5 All  Entrepreneurship  Event  /  Startup  Pitch events  participation  shall  be

recommended by Participation Committee which includes (list mentions the

name in descending order of signature and remarks required) 

3.1.3.5.1 Head, LPU Startup School

3.1.3.5.2 Head, Division of Student Welfare

3.1.3.5.3 Division of Research and Development (for any idea with a potential IP)

Page | 6 



3.1.3.5.4 Respective School HOS

3.1.3.5.5 Respective School Entrepreneurship Coach

3.1.4 The application should contain:

3.1.4.1 A cover letter requesting off-campus participation.

3.1.4.2 Details  of  all  the  off-campus  participations  done  by  student  in  the  same

academic year in which facilities are provided by University.

3.1.4.3 A record  of  the  past  performances/  achievements/  prizes  achieved  by  the

student in similar events.

3.1.4.4 Copy  of  the  event  invitation  letter  or  advertisement  posted  including

information regarding date, time, venue, registration charges, prizes and other

terms and conditions.

3.1.4.5 Parent consent letter of all the participants (Annexure II).

3.1.4.6 Detail of all the team members and requested duty leaves as per the format

(Annexure III)

3.1.4.7 All the resource requirements are to be submitted as per (Annexure IV). This

list consists of total requirements for the event and not only the requirements

asked  from  the  University.  This  annexure  does  not  apply  to  applicants

pertaining to Category III and IV facilitation.

3.1.4.8 An undertaking confirming that no disciplinary action has been taken against

the student in past and he/she is not under disciplinary probation at present.

3.1.4.9 References (if any).

3.1.5 University is not responsible for intimation about any off-campus event. Students

are  themselves  responsible  for  keeping  track  of  off-campus  events  and  the

deadlines.

3.1.6 University  is  not  responsible  for  approval  of  any  such  application  which  is

submitted less than 15 days before the event.
Page | 7 



3.1.7 The sanctioning may take up to 7 days depending upon the case and the facilities

required.

3.1.8 Sanction if any can be withdrawn anytime before the commencement of event

without assigning any reason.

3.2 Selection Rules

3.2.1 Institutes/  Universities  and  events  in  which  students  would  be  facilitated  and

funded for off-campus participation will be at the discretion of recommending &

sanctioning authorities.

3.2.2 Only one team per Discipline (including all constituent Schools) per activity/item

may be selected. In case, the recommending authorities find more than one team

competent enough to be sent then they can recommend the same to approving

authority as a special case.

3.2.3 Students, who are selected for participating in an on-campus or off-campus event

by University authorities, are not allowed to take part in any other off-campus

event at their own discretion during the practice and the participation period as

stated by concerned authorities, until unless permitted by University authorities.

3.2.4 A student could be funded maximum 3 times in a year only.

3.3 Rules for Duty Leaves, Funds and Facilities

3.3.1 Duty Leaves shall be provided as per the ‚ÄòDuty Leave Policy‚Äô.

3.3.2 The decision to provide facilities will depend on the past performance of students,

facilities availed by student in past, quality of the event and the institute hosting it,

relevant references from any Department(s) / Cell(s). 

Page | 8 



3.3.3 For  Category  II  events,  funds  recommended  may  vary  from  30%  to  70%

depending upon the level of event, capability of student and funding provisions of

University. Students will have to manage the rest of requirements by themselves.

3.3.4 An event  may  be  considered  under  Category  II  only  if  the  name  of  hosting

Institute/  University/  Agency is  mentioned in the approved list  as provided in

Appendix A. Any other  event  shall  be considered under Category III  only.  A

event or hosting Institute/ University/ Agency may be added to Appendix A on

forwarding  the  same  to  Participation  Committees  and  on  approval  of  Pro-

Chancellor.

3.3.5 Any requirement  requested will  be approved on merits  of the case and at  the

entire discretion of the concerned authority. The decision of the authority will be

final and binding. Guidelines for selection are mentioned in Appendix B.

3.3.6 Half of the approved funds sanctioned will be provided in advance and the rest

will  be  provided  as  a  reimbursement  to  the  expenses  on  submission  of  the

authentic bills.

3.3.7 TA/DA, if sanctioned, shall be provided as per the limits mentioned in 

Appendix C.

3.3.8 Students  are  themselves  responsible  for  arrangements  regarding  transportation

reservations etc.

3.3.9 Student(s) if sponsored by some external agency for the participation shall have to

disclose such endorsements in writing along with the application.

3.4 Reimbursement and after Event formalities

Page | 9 



3.4.1 Student availing the Funds will have to submit authentic bills equating the amount

funded within 3 working days after the return from the event. The bills should be

in accordance to the budget approved. Any loss due to non-availability of bills,

non-authentic bills  or mismatch in budget approved and bills  provided will  be

suffered by beneficiary of Funds and not by University.

3.4.2 Properties,  if  funded,  will  have  to  be  submitted  back  to  Division  of  Student

Welfare Store.

3.4.3 A report should be submitted providing the details about the event, participation,

achievement, learning and experiences (Annexure IV).

Appendix VII
(Entrepreneurship/Startup)

The list of long term courses runs by LPU Startup School
1. Entrepreneurship Development Program ‚Äì Weekend Course (10 Weekends every Term)

a) Offered Every Term
